<review>Has a beautiful view of Yosemite. You can drive here. There is plenty of parking it is a small walk from your car to the observation deck area there are so many different areas for great pictures. If you want to see all the waterfalls go in June when there are the fullest. There is a small gift shop and little place to get coffee and lunch. This would have gotten 5 stars however both times I have been here ( a year apart) the restooms at this stop are in the least a health risk for anyone! I have seen men go out in the woods right near the restrooms and parking lot just to avoid using the facility and ladies just hold it for the hour trip back to Yosemite valley. This needs to be taken care of!!!</review><username>Amber Brooks</username></record>

< Text>
(Translated by Google) Unmissable beautiful observation point on the Yosemiti Valley with the Half Dome in the background. Well-kept place like all American parks. Breath-taking view. (Translated by Google) Glacier Point: The glacier tops are vast, especially at sunset or full moon nights, and the smooth granite walls exude magical charm. From here, the 3,200-foot-high cliff overlooks the Yosemite Valley. Opposite the valley, Yosemite Falls rushed down. Looking at the High Sierra, the world is vast and boundless.
There are trails leading to other attractions in the valley that overlook the scenery. In the summer, you can drive from the Yosemite Valley to the top of the glacier, 32 miles (one hour drive). In the winter, the road above the Badger Pass Ski Area is closed, and the top of the glacier is the most popular cross-country skiing terminal.

However, I‚Äôm staying in the area for a few weeks and my dog needed to be groomed.

Onto my experience, I took my dog in at 10 AM on the dot day of appt. One issue is the fact that I did not receive word of my dog until 2:15 PM. It took almost four and a half hours to finish grooming my dog. The business should allocate time properly and be done with grooming in a timely manner. The was hoping to see some paranormal book stacking or recto-plastic residue but The foyer is so nice it almost makes you forget about the exterior view. If I lived in CA I would be sure to make an effort to come here at least a few times a month. < Review>
I had to go and change my review since I've been here for the last 2 months and I have to admit what I said about the quality of Education here is absolutely correct the staff the teachers are wonderful. However here are a few things that you should know that they don't actually tell you in orientation.  Rule number one if you were an out-of-state resident go someplace else. If you have previous student loans you may not be able to get financial aid here or at least a long portion of it. The school has a $20,000 aggregate loan limit for financial aid. And the one thing that they don't tell you is that the real person who actually runs the campus has to be the actual police chief and if you think this is a joke it's not. Hours from things like libraries and so forth are very limited. The other thing that was really all this is that they actually have a proxy server that limits your ability to go ahead and use the network services like for example log me in remote login services that you may need for some of your classes. I honestly have to say if they got rid of the campus police I would absolutely give this place four and a half Stars. However if you're an actual resident of California this place is a complete five-star Institution. However with the recent meetings and the last guy that actually broke both of his wrists and was actually punched in the back of the head I would highly discourage  taking any of those political studies courses here, it's not a good idea.<//Review>

< Text>
[from Aug 2006]

WARNING WARNING WARNING
Overeducated-snob alert!
*  *  *

I've taken three classes at City College.
The first -- an intermediate level dance class -- was taught by a very capable and caring instructor, but far too many people selfishly took this class despite (knowingly) not even knowing the basics. "I couldn't fit the beginning class into my schedule, and I wanted an easy 'A'" said one of them.  Jerk.

The second was taught by an instructor who was moderately proficient in her subject, but seemed at least a bit burnt out.

The third class was taught by a decently smart and dedicated fellow, but the ambience felt so much like high school, I almost ran screaming out into the parking lot after the first week.  Reminders not to chew gum, the taking of attendance... it was clear that a lot of the kids here were just grudgingly fulfilling their language requirement and had no passion for learning another language.

Indeed, that is my biggest gripe about this place.  Passion.  Walking around campus, sitting in classes... it just feels like folks are going through the promotions.  Trying to get into a better school.  Taking classes because their parents are forcing them to.  Love of learning?  I sure didn't see a whole lot of it.  And after my mostly-inspiring years in undergrad and grad school... this was all rather bleak and depressing.

*  *  *

So why THREE stars?  Well, I feel that affordable education should be available to everyone.   The campus is pretty accessible by public transit.  And at least a couple of the CCSF instructors I've met are cool people.<//Text>

<Name>Haley Carter</Name><Date>1627404102824< /Date>< rate>
4<//rate>
< review>
Comfortable and peaceful -- my mom and I visited for a basic mani/pedi, and really liked sitting on a comfortable antique sofa, soaking our feet in large copper basins.

The nail stylists (is that the proper reference?) were friendly and welcoming. It seemed that all the other patrons were regular customers. My mom and I were visiting from out of town and were referred by a friend.

It was the luck of the draw that my stylist was experienced at both the body mechanics of enjoyable foot and leg message, along with tending well to the proper care of callouses, cuticles, nail beds, and the cosmetic aspects of painting nails. Several days later, and I still like the way my hands and feet look and feel.

My mom, however, wasn't as lucky, and it seems her stylist was fairly inexperienced. The foot and leg massage was tentative, and the actual application of polish was uneven and not really up to par.

That said, we both left the salon feeling relaxed and cared for. I will return, should I be in the area again.

EDIT TO ADD:
The owner/manager called and kindly offered my mom another manicure, though we weren't able to follow through to schedule. I greatly appreciate the gesture, and that confirms that I will return when I'm back in the area again.<//review>

< review>
Wanted to share my experience.  I ordered a to-go item with butter nan.  I picked up the item and by the time I reached home (around 10 mins), I noticed that Nan had become very hard and was not edible.  I could not eat it.  I called this restaurant to inform about the the Nan.  I was expecting an apology.  Instead of that the manager (I think name was Samar or something) started kind of lecturing me that Nans are made that way as If I have never eaten one.  The tone of manager was as if customer was lying about problem with Nan.  I understand that there are subjective things such as taste of food  etc where you could argue with customer (even then it is a bad idea),  but Nan being too hard is demonstrable fact and there was no need to argue.

A very basic rule in restaurant business is (or any business) to hear customer's criticism and improve.  Also if customer is calling about the quality of food or service,  make amends and not argue.  Any restaurant business that blames customers for quality of food does not know the basic rules of running restaurant business.

I think owner of this business has hired incompetent manager and other staff to run his business.  Unhappy customers would go to other places specially in Bay area where there is no shortage of Indian restaurants.< /review>

<gmap_id>0x808f9e80addce7cb:0x174b3f24aa964a62</gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
<text>This rating is based solely off of one dish that they prepare: Vijayawada Chicken Biryani, aka the best Biryani in the Bay area and arguably my entire Biryani experience.

If you're from the area, you know how many options there are for good Indian food, so you'll understand when I say that I only go to each place for a couple exemplary dishes (not the whole menu). Well for Tabla, that's the Biryani mentioned above!

Don't come for the dining experience, the ambiance, the service or the music. Come for the only thing that matters here, the Biryani!

The aroma is enticing, smelling strongly of a refined selection of rich Indian spices. Unlike many styles, this one has the rice on top and the chicken baked underneath (of which there is a surprisingly good amount). Large portions, soaked in a fantastic curry accompaniment, you just can't go wrong with this one. The spice level is great - not too much so as to make those with low tolerances cry but enough to make the more acclimated stop intermittently and appreciate the flavor (while giving their tongue a quick rest). Plus the raita is perfect to help relieve the burn (and alleviate digestion troubles by protectively lining the stomach).

As mentioned, I can't speak towards the dining experience, or really the rest of the menu (except for some unsurprisingly mediocre tandoori chicken).

My sole recommendation is that you order the Vijayawada Chicken Biryani! And if you're like me, get an extra to go (because it only gets better).< /text>< user>

Reducing to 3 stars. I have been here 5-6 times during lunch and every time I have experienced it.
The pressure cooker whistle starts off all of a sudden and its pretty loud. It goes on for a minute at a stretch at least. And it goes off 4 -5 times one after the other. I think you can imagine how the experience gets like when you are eating and at times it gets too annoying. You can't even hear what's the guy next to you is saying.

ORIGINAL REVIEW
----------------------------
Quite a bit of food in the price.
They have complimentary Indian milk tea as well which tastes great.

I was not able to complete the thali and the food tasted great.
I was happy to see that they serve fresh chapati as well. The seats and tables needs to be lot more cleaner.
